[{"id":32257,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/2019-20-nba-schedule-notebook","date":"2019-08-14","title":"Schedule notebook: First 20 games can make (or break) a playoff push","content":" There are 1,230 games in an NBA season and while it may seem like there\u2019s a lot of season left when the calendar flips from November to December, what we\u2019ve already seen at that point will tell us a lot. Over the last 20 (full) seasons, there has been a strong correlation between a team\u2019s record after 20 games and its record at the end of the season. Really, there\u2019s a pretty strong correlation between a team\u2019s record after just 10 games and how it finishes the season. The correlation grows with each game and the 20-game mark isn\u2019t a significant inflection point in that regard. It is 1\/4 of the way through the season and a benchmark that many teams use to take measure of just what kind of team they are. Like, if you haven\u2019t won at least seven of those first 20 games, you\u2019re most certainly not going to make the playoffs. Only four of the 106 teams that have won fewer than seven of their first 20 games over the last 20 (full) seasons have gone on to reach the postseason. The last of those was the 2013-14 Brooklyn Nets, who started 6-14, finished as the No. 6 seed in the East (at 44-38) , and actually won a first-round series. On the other end of the spectrum, 92 percent of the 215 teams that have won at least 12 of their first 20 games have gone on to make the playoffs. That translates to about one miss per year, with last season\u2019s Memphis Grizzlies (who started 12-8) and the 2017-18 Detroit Pistons (the only Eastern Conference team of the last 20 full seasons that has won 14 of its first 20 games and failed to make the playoffs) being the latest two examples. * Smith: Key dates to know for 2019-20 The Grizzlies didn\u2019t have that easy of an early schedule last season. Eleven of their first 20 games were against teams that finished with winning records, and 10 of their first 20 were on the road. They obviously couldn\u2019t keep it together after a strong start, but their \u201918-19 season was more the exception than the rule. The schedule eventually balances itself out, but every team wants to get off to a good start. And some will have an easier time than others. The New Orleans Pelicans and Oklahoma City Thunder are two of the league\u2019s more interesting teams on paper. Both teams traded their best players, but they each still have a seemingly competent rotation remaining. If the pieces \u2014 both young and old \u2014 come together in the right way, either (or both) of these teams could be competing for playoff spots. But to remain relevant through the All-Star break, the Pelicans and Thunder will have to survive the league\u2019s two toughest schedules through 20 games. There were 15 teams that had winning records last season. All but two of the league\u2019s 30 teams will play no more than 12 of their first 20 games against that group, and the two exceptions are the Pelicans and Thunder. The Pelicans will play 15 of their first 20 games against teams that had winning records last season. One of the other five will be against against the Los Angeles Lakers, who (with former Pelican Anthony Davis) are very likely to finish with a winning record this season. And New Orleans will play four of its 12 back-to-backs within those first 20 games. The Thunder, meanwhile, will play 14 of their first 20 games against teams that had winning records last season. Two of their other six will be against the Lakers. And within that first 20 games, they will have three *rest-disadvantage games, but just one rest-advantage game. * A rest advantage or disadvantage is when one team is playing the second game of a back-to-back and the other didn\u2019t play the day before. Here are the records of home teams over the last three seasons\u2026 Interestingly, the Pelicans and Thunder will play each other three times \u2014 twice in Oklahoma City and once in New Orleans \u2014 within their first 20 games, with a home-and-home series on Nov. 29 and Dec. 1. If one team is struggling to get it together early on, the other could take advantage. The toughest first 20 games in the Eastern Conference \u2014 when taking opponents, home vs. road, and rest into account \u2014 belongs to the Atlanta Hawks . The Hawks were, statistically, the league\u2019s fourth-most improved team after the All-Star break last season. Given the strength of their first 20 games in \u201919-20, it will be tough for them to turn that into a stronger start this year. The Hawks\u2019 first 20 games include 13 games (most in the East) against teams that finished at or above .500 last season and 11 road games. Five of those 11 are part of a trip (their longest of the season) that concludes with an L.A.-L.A. back-to-back, one of five back-to-backs (most in the league) that the Hawks will have in their first 20 games. The second games of four of those five back-to-backs will be rest-disadvantage games, but the Hawks will have just one rest-advantage game (their first game of the season) in their first 20. The Denver Nuggets are set to lead the league in continuity, with more than 92 percent of last season\u2019s minutes having been played by guys who are still on the roster. And that\u2019s not the only thing that could allow them to hit the ground running. In regard to the cumulative 2018-19 winning percentage of their opponents, the Nuggets have the league\u2019s easiest first 20 games. They\u2019ll play 13 of their first 20 games (most in the league) against teams that had losing records last season . One of the other seven will be against the Lakers, but that game (on Dec. 3) will be in Denver, where the Nuggets will play 11 of their first 18 before heading East for a four-game trip. Last season, the Nuggets were 13.1 points per 100 possessions better at home than on the road, and that was the league\u2019s biggest differential. Overall, the first 20 games is balanced in regard to home-away. Only six of the league\u2019s 30 teams don\u2019t have at least nine home games and at least nine road games in their first 20. The league has once again reduced the average number of back-to-backs for each team. This season, the average is 12.4 back-to-backs per team, down from 13.3 last season and 19.3 five years ago. Teams will have no fewer than 11 and no more than 14 back-to-backs. Last season, the range was 12-15, and in 2014-15, it was 16-22. There\u2019s been less of a reduction in rest-advantage games, from 300 last season to 293 this season. That\u2019s still an all-time low, but there remains a bigger variance in the number of rest-advantage (and rest-disadvantage) games than there is in the number of back-to-backs. While the back-to-back range is 12-15, teams have as few as five and as many as 16 rest-advantage games. They also have as few as five and as many as 13 rest-disadvantage games. On the low end of the former is the Orlando Magic , who have a league-low five rest-advantage games (and one of the five is the last game of the season). The New York Knicks , meanwhile, have 16, including two four-game stretches (one in November and one going into the All-Star break) where they\u2019ll have three rest-advantage games. The Chicago Bulls have a league-low five rest-disadvantage games, and the first one isn\u2019t until Jan. 11 (Game 40) in Detroit. In fact, in none of the Bulls \u2018 first 25 games will either team have a rest advantage. The Cleveland Cavaliers and Phoenix Suns have the most rest-disadvantage games (13). The Suns have three in a seven-game stretch in December, while the Cavs have four in their first 13 games after the All-Star break. If you subtract rest-disadvantage games from rest-advantage games to get an overall \u201crest advantage factor\u201d for each team\u2019s 82 games, the Bulls (11 rest-advantage games, five rest-disadvantage games) and Knicks (16, 10) have the easiest schedule, with no other team having a differential greater than three. The Magic (five, 10) and Washington Wizards (seven, 12) have the biggest differentials in the other direction.   * * * John Schuhmann is a senior stats analyst for NBA.com. We look forward to him bringing those qualities to our front office.\u201d Jamison joins the Wizards\u2019 front office after spending the past two seasons as a scout for the Los Angeles Lakers. He will work with vice president of pro personnel Johnny Rogers on the organization\u2019s NBA and G League scouting as well as the team\u2019s international scouting efforts. Jamison played for the Wizards for six seasons (2004-10), posting averages of 20.8 points and 8.9 rebounds and earning two All-Star selections with Washington. The 17-year NBA pro averaged 18.5 points and 7.5 rebounds in 1,083 career games (864 starts) with Golden State, Dallas, Washington, Cleveland, the Los Angeles Lakers and Los Angeles Clippers. Jamison played collegiately at the University of North Carolina where he won the Wooden and Naismith Awards as the most outstanding college basketball player as a junior during the 1997-98 season. He was originally selected fourth overall by the Toronto Raptors in the 1998 NBA Draft. Profit, a four-year NBA veteran, enjoyed two stints with the Wizards (1999-01, 2004-05). During his NBA career, he appeared in 135 games (18 starts) and averaged 3.3 points and 1.5 rebounds with the Wizards and Lakers. Originally selected 38th overall by Orlando out of the University of Maryland in the 1999 NBA Draft, Profit last served in the NBA in an assistant coach\/player development role with the Magic from 2012-16. Carideo spent the 2018-19 season as a pro and college scout with the Memphis Grizzlies. They will reflect on the greatness, the fun, all they learned from each other shooting side by side day after day. Two championships, a pair of NBA Finals MVP awards for Durant. \u201cI\u2019ll always remember the three years we had. We\u2019ll probably be back here down the road celebrating those like they did the \u201974-75 team,\u201d Curry said, nodding in the direction of the Warriors\u2019 recent championship banners. \u201cIt\u2019ll be cool when that happens.\u201d For now, Curry is embracing \u201cnew beginnings\u201d as the oldest player on a Golden State roster that will look far different come training camp next month \u2014 and that also was the theme he shared with girls attending his Warriors camp this week in one of his \u201cbittersweet\u201d final trips to the downtown Oakland practice facility before a move to San Francisco and the new Chase Center. Durant, recovering from surgery to repair a ruptured right Achilles tendon, has departed to join the Brooklyn Nets. \u201cWe won two championships and I think we both got better throughout the process as basketball players and as people,\u201d Curry said. \u201cWith the demand every single night to be great and just all that that comes with, in terms of the media attention, the scrutiny, the criticism, the praise even, it\u2019s a lot to handle. And I think me and him especially on that level could connect. Him going to Brooklyn, you\u2019re just trying to make sure he\u2019s happy and going to a place where he feels like he needs to be. At the end of the day, you\u2019ve got to be happy about that for him.\u201d Also gone are veterans Andre Iguodala and Shaun Livingston, guard Quinn Cook and big man DeMarcus Cousins. Meanwhile, the Warriors have added a handful of new faces like D\u2019Angelo Russell, Willie Cauley-Stein and Glenn Robinson III. Draymond Green got a new four-year deal earlier this month worth close to $100 million. Kevon Looney re-signed, too. As Klay Thompson works back this season from surgery for a torn ACL in his left knee that he injured in the deciding Game 6 loss of the finals to the Toronto Raptors, Curry\u2019s backcourt mate will be Russell. At 31, Curry doesn\u2019t mind that he will be the quote-unquote old guy entering his 11th NBA season. A two-time NBA MVP, he has reached five straight NBA Finals. \u201cHas it sunk in? No. Have people been reminding me? Yes, any time they bring up our team looking forward,\u201d he said with a smile. \u201cIt\u2019s cool though, hopefully I\u2019m wise beyond my years but still youthful in what I can do on the floor. It\u2019s just a change in dynamic all the way around. We\u2019re excited about the opportunities, the challenges for the whole roster, because we\u2019ve got a lot of guys that have the opportunity to really prove themselves and make a difference in our team. Obviously our core, \u2019til Klay gets back, we know how to win and we know how to play. We\u2019re just going to do it a little differently.\u201d Curry is unconcerned at this stage about outside expectations regarding how good this group might be and speculation that these Warriors may not be a championship contender. \u201cI know the reality of the situation in terms of we lost a guy like Kevin Durant, who\u2019s an all-time great basketball player,\u201d Curry said. \u201cWe lost two veteran high-IQ guys in Shaun and Andre that really were like the cogs in the wheel that kept us going and you could rely on them every single game. So, the look is different but nobody really has a sustained run like we did where every year you\u2019re expected to be the greatest. It\u2019s just a matter of now we have to, I wouldn\u2019t even say prove people wrong, but we have to kind of galvanize the new roster and do the exact same thing.\u201d As he told the girl campers all sporting his No. 30 jersey, first things first. Curry took a quick poll of how many had started school again. Dozens of hands shot into the air. \u201cGreat to see you all again! You all having a great day, too?\u201d Collective \u201cYeah!\u201d \u201cNew beginnings, right? We\u2019re going to take care of our school work this year?\u201d Curry asked. \u201cWe\u2019re going to be very dedicated and hard-working in the classroom as we are on the basketball court? That\u2019s very important to be well-rounded people, right? How many for the Warriors?   * * * Steve Aschburner : Toronto was 17-5 on the nights Kawhi Leonard did not play last season, but selectively choosing his absences is different from enduring them across all 82 games. Golden State was 1-0 when playing without both Kevin Durant and Klay Thompson, a throwaway of No. 81 that offers no insight into how the Warriors will fare without the former at all in 2019-20 and the latter for a good chunk of the schedule. I think both teams are wired to top .500, though, and make the playoffs as lower seeds \u2014 the Warriors winning 45-47 times and the Raptors around 42-43 victories (assuming they don\u2019t pull the plug by the trade deadline). Shaun Powell :  The East isn\u2019t exactly loaded, so even without Kawhi Leonard, the Raptors should knock on the door of 50 wins (but l et\u2019s put them a few short, say 48). As for the Warriors sans Durant, that\u2019s a tougher chore in the big-boy West, and there\u2019s no telling when Thompson suits up or how D\u2019Angelo Russell clicks with Stephen Curry. This smells like 47 wins for Golden State, and maybe that\u2019s giving them too much respect. John Schuhmann : The Raptors were an amazing 17-5 without Leonard last season, but they also had Danny Green, who was a huge part of that no-Kawhi success. Pascal Siakam and OG Anunoby should only get better, but it\u2019s also possible that Raptors GM Masai Ujiri will trade some of his vets on expiring contracts rather than lose them for nothing next summer. Even if he keeps the group together, the Raptors will take a step backward, landing in the 46-50-win range . With Thompson out, the Warriors have a lot more questions than answers on the wings, especially if D\u2019Angelo Russell isn\u2019t a good fit in coach Steve Kerr\u2019s offense. But they still have Curry and Draymond Green, who are keystones to an elite offense and defense, respectively. This feels hard to peg down than a prediction for the Raptors, because chemistry is more of a question, but put the Western Conference champs in the same 46-50-win range .  Sekou Smith : Even with Kawhi Leonard having for the Western Conference, the Toronto Raptors will have enough to be one of the more formidable teams in the Eastern Conference. A 47-50 win season is a reasonable expectation for the reigning champs , who should be a bunch toughened up by the things they experienced during their championship run. No team lost more firepower from last season than the Warriors, who will open the Chase Center without Durant, Thompson (inured), Andre Iguodala (traded), DeMarcus Cousins (signed with Lakers) and Shaun Livingston (waived). But I\u2019ll keep it simple and go with the most additional victories in 2019-20 compared to last season. For me, then, the choice is easy: the Lakers. They are going to clean up multiple messes \u2014 no finishing below .500 this time, no missing the postseason \u2014 and add 20 victories while shaving 20 losses from their 37-45 record. LeBron James will have had a long offseason \u2014 basketball-wise, at least \u2014 and quite possibly be primed for a monstrous individual performance in the year he turns 35. John Schuhmann :  The Clippers and Lakers are the obvious picks to make the biggest jumps in the win column. But he\u2019s getting a huge dose of it now and for the foreseeable future. As one of the veteran leaders in camp as the U.S. Men\u2019s Senior National Team prepares for the FIBA World Cup , he\u2019s living that role every day. And he\u2019s doing it alongside three of his younger USA teammates \u2014 Jayson Tatum, Jaylen Brown and Marcus Smart \u2014 he\u2019ll work with in Boston when the 2019-20 NBA season begins. This opportunity to fine-tune their chemistry and build camaraderie ahead of next season is one of the benefits of their time together this summer. Walker said as much as Team USA wrapped up practice Tuesday night at the UCLA Health Training Center. \u201cThey\u2019re just some really good young dudes and I just enjoy being around them,\u201d Walker said. \u201cAnd the age difference is really crazy to me. J.T. is like 21 and J.B. is 22 and Marcus is 25. And I\u2019m 29 and feeling like, wow, this is cool. It sounds crazy. I remember when I was 21 in this league. I was a rookie and just trying to figure it all out. And these guys are young vets already. Like I said, it\u2019s crazy.\u201d And ideal if you are Celtics\u2019 boss Danny Ainge, who attended Tuesday\u2019s practice, or Celtics coach Brad Stevens. The bonds developed now will help forge a brotherhood that was clearly missing last season. Chemistry issues sank the Celtics\u2019 hopes of contending for a third straight trip to the Eastern Conference finals in what turned out to be Kyrie Irving and Al Horford\u2019s final season in Boston. Given all that the Celtics\u2019 quartet is learning about each other this summer, chemistry shouldn\u2019t be a problem. Walker praised his young teammates for their diligence and work ethic while marveling at their ability to pick up the nuances and changes that comprise FIBA World Cup play. \u201cEverybody comes here knowing they\u2019ll have to sacrifice some of the things they are used to doing for the greater good and they get that,\u201d Walker said. \u201cAnd for me, having some experience and being one of the older guys here, it\u2019s a great opportunity to show some leadership and also humble myself in this process. But the chance for these young guys to showcase their talents is really dope. I\u2019m glad to be here with someone like [U.S. Coach Gregg Popovich] running it and to be a part of it, because normally these are guys I\u2019m battling with every night and now we get a chance to work together. The sky is the limit for what they can do and I just love being a part of this stage of it all.\u201d Tatum, Brown and Smart have each gained insight into Walker\u2019s game as well \u2014 in particular what it\u2019s like to see the All-Star guard work every day. \u201cFor me, I\u2019ve noticed that Kemba can really play defense when he wants to do it,\u201d Smart said and then laughed. \u201cYou know it\u2019s tough, when you see how much energy he had to exert on the offensive end [in Charlotte], but he\u2019s actually a really good defensive player, especially at his size. You find out that the little guys are usually more feisty and tenacious. But he can play defense and you didn\u2019t really see that or notice that because he had so much of a load on him offensively that it was probably harder for him to do that.\u201d Smart agreed with Walker\u2019s point about everyone here in camp having to play roles as opposed to focusing on what they might be used to on their respective NBA teams. \u201cWe\u2019ve got a lot of guys who on their respective teams are the man or whatever you want to call it,\u201d Smart said. \u201cThey\u2019re either the first, second or third option on their team and here they might not even be fourth or fifth. It takes a lot of humility to look yourself in the face and say, \u2018okay, what does this team need from me?\u2019 And be ready to do it. If it means stepping outside of what I do normally, that\u2019s okay. That\u2019s what we\u2019re here for. And that\u2019s what this [USA Basketball] environment brings out of all of us.\u201d Smart was the only member of the team in sweats Tuesday night as he\u2019s still dealing with the sore left calf that cost him the final three days of last week\u2019s camp in Las Vegas. He could return to the court by the end of the week. He said he hopes to be ready for Friday night\u2019s exhibition game against Spain in Anaheim. \u201cI don\u2019t know for sure when\u201d he said. \u201cIt\u2019s just a matter of getting it right.\u201d No return fire from Pop  Popovich isn\u2019t interested in any verbal sparring ahead of the competition. He\u2019s got more important things to worry about than responding to any shots fired from opposing coaches. When asked for his thoughts on Serbian coach Aleksandar \u201cSasha\u201d Djordjevic saying if his team were to face the U.S. team in China, \u201cmay God help them,\u201d Pop kept didn\u2019t bite. \u201cI don\u2019t really pay attention to much, I\u2019ve been doing this for too long,\u201d Popovich said. \u201cHe\u2019s a hell of a coach, he\u2019s a competitor and he\u2019s been a hero in Europe, you know, as a player. He was fantastic. And he has a program that goes way back with lots of success. And they do have a heck of a team. There\u2019s no doubt about that. They are deep, they are talented and they are going to work their fannies off. And they want to win, just like we do or anybody else who is in the tournament. You know, people will talk, but that\u2019s usually not something I respond to.\u201d * * * Sekou Smith is a veteran NBA reporter and NBA TV analyst. Telfair \u2014 a once highly touted point guard with a disappointing pro basketball career and a history of brushes with the law \u2014 had been convicted earlier this year of carrying a loaded handgun in his pickup truck. \u201cThe mandatory prison sentence he received today is required by law and he has now been held accountable for the unlawful conduct,\u201d Brooklyn District Attorney Eric Gonzalez said in a statement. There was no immediate response to a phone message on Monday seeking comment from Telfair\u2019s attorney. Gonzalez said that a jury heard testimony describing how at 2:50 a.m. on June 11, 2017, officers in an unmarked police car spotted a Ford F-150 parked on a center median in Brooklyn with the 34-year-old Telfair at the wheel. The officers stopped the truck after it made a U-turn in front of them and drove off with no headlights on. Seeing a lit marijuana cigarette in the console, they said they searched the vehicle and found a loaded .45-caliber pistol inside. The Brooklyn-born Telfair was a first-round draft pick out of high school in 2004. He started with the Portland Trail Blazers and spent time with the Boston Celtics, Minnesota Timberwolves and other teams before ending his career in China in 2014. Telfair and a friend were arrested in 2007 after a traffic stop during which police found a loaded handgun in the vehicle. Rookies, rivalries, redemption stories, return games and all the drama that comes along with that litany of storylines are on tap for the 2019-20 season. And with Monday\u2019s release of the full \u201919-20 season schedule , we can all begin to plot our own course through what promises to be a wildly entertaining \u2014 and unpredictable \u2014 season. For the first time in years there is no clear-cut, prohibitive favorite to win the Larry O\u2019Brien championship trophy. Some have even proclaimed the \u201cSuper Team\u201d era over. The list of teams who fancy themselves true championship contenders is as long as it\u2019s been in recent seasons, and perhaps ever, which is the real treat for everyone. With that in mind, here are just some of the must-watch dates we have circled on the NBA calendar (and further study will certainly provide more). (Note: The games are listed in no particular order and each is followed by an explanation as to why it made the list): Oct. 22 New Orleans Pelicans vs. Toronto Raptors (8 p.m. ET, TNT) Los Angeles Lakers vs. LA Clippers (10:30 p.m. ET, TNT) Why we\u2019re tuning in: How could you do anything else on opening night? We get our first glimpse at No. 1 overall pick Zion Williamson and the revamped Pelicans traveling north of the border on ring and banner night for Kyle Lowry, Pascal Siakam and the reigning champion Raptors. Then we get to top it off with the first taste of the battle for L.A. between the Staples Center roomies expected to pace the Western Conference this season. The Clippers are technically the home team, but we\u2019ll see if it feels like a Clippers or Lakers building that night. The best part is we don\u2019t have to wait to see how LeBron James and Anthony Davis match up against Kawhi Leonard and Paul George. Dec. 11 LA Clippers vs. Toronto Raptors (7 p.m. ET, ESPN) Why we\u2019re tuning in: What do you get the man who delivered it all in his one season in Toronto in his first trip back with his new crew? Knowing what we do of Raptors fans, it\u2019ll be a raucous standing ovation as they pay their respects to Leonard before trying to take the Clippers apart (as Fred Van Vleet promised when asked what they\u2019d do if Kawhi left in free agency). You don\u2019t wait as long as the Raptors did for that championship parade and let Kawhi\u2019s decision to go home spoil the moment. In the end, everyone got what they wanted out of that short-term fling. This night will provide the closure that will allow Raptors fans to move on. Nov. 27 Brooklyn Nets vs. Boston Celtics (7 p.m. ET, ESPN) Los Angeles Lakers vs. New Orleans Pelicans (9:30 p.m. ET, ESPN) Why we\u2019re tuning in: Nobody does big-stage drama better than Kyrie Irving, whose first trip back to Boston against his old teammates without Kevin Durant in uniform will be a show-and-prove night for all involved. Irving is carrying the Nets on his shoulders until Durant returns. The Celtics\u2019 youngsters will be eager to show him that they\u2019re better off with Kemba Walker in his place anyway. The fact that these are division rivals who could be battling for playoff positioning all season won\u2019t even be a factor on this night. This is sure to be a good old fashioned grudge match. On the same night Irving goes back to boos in Boston, Davis will face something similar in the Big Easy. Pelicans fans didn\u2019t hide their disdain for Davis once they learned of his trade request last season. His departure for the Lakers, even with all the Pelicans got in return, won\u2019t be enough to soften the mood upon his return to the city he called home for the first seven season of his career. The former Lakers shipped out to acquire Davis \u2014 Lonzo Ball, Brandon Ingram and Josh Hart \u2014 will surely get up for this game as well. Dec. 22 LA Clippers vs. Oklahoma City Thunder (7 p.m. ET, NBA TV) Why we\u2019re tuning in: George\u2019s trade request to the Clippers, is still a tough pill for Thunder fans to swallow. It hastened Russell Westbrook\u2019s departure and the franchise reboot that\u2019s to come. But George will be greeted by Chris Paul, taking on one of his former teams as well, and a Thunder group that will use every slight, real and imagined, to fuel their fire this season. Jan. 9 Houston Rockets vs. Oklahoma City Thunder (9:30 p.m. ET, TNT) Why we\u2019re tuning in: This one could get emotional, for Westbrook and what will certainly be a sellout, standing-room-only crowd that fills the building for his return to his old stomping grounds. Things didn\u2019t end the way anyone envisioned. Westbrook fancied himself a Thunder lifer and an adopted Oklahoman, only to see it all come apart with Leonard\u2019s summer power play with the Clippers. That tribute video the Thunder cook up for Westbrook\u2019s return should be epic. Nov. 7 Boston Celtics vs. Charlotte Hornets (8 ET, p.m. TNT) Why we\u2019re tuning in: Walker was the face of the franchise for years in Charlotte but once again, the free agent frenzy of 2019 showed that indeed nothing lasts forever. He\u2019s sure to receive the hero\u2019s welcome upon returning to the city for the first time in green and white. His replacement, former Celtics point guard Terry Rozier, probably has other plans for how he wants things to go. But it\u2019ll be tough for anyone to spoil the moment for a player who was as beloved as Walker was by fans in the Queen City. Nov. 15 Utah Jazz vs. Memphis Grizzlies (8 p.m. ET, ESPN) Why we\u2019re tuning in: Mike Conley\u2019s tenure in Memphis helped define an era in a basketball-mad region of the country. Folks in the mid-South will be talking about the Grit-and-Grind Grizzlies for years to come and Conley is in line for one of those tear-jerker, team-made tribute videos. But he doesn\u2019t need anyone\u2019s pity, not with the Jazz team he\u2019ll captain this season. They are primed for a breakout year with Conley and Donovan Mitchell leading the way in one of the league\u2019s most complete backcourts. The Grizzlies, meanwhile, hope they have their next Conley-Marc Gasol duo in place with rookie point guard Ja Morant and second-year big man Jaren Jackson Jr. Oct. 23 Boston Celtics vs. Philadelphia 76ers (7:30 p.m. ET, ESPN) Why we\u2019re tuning in: The Celtics and Sixers were both at times last year the hot pick to be kings of the East, only to see the Raptors snatch the mantle in the playoffs. Now we get an early look at both teams, with tweaks, of course (Kemba in place of Kyrie in Boston; Al Horford as the grown up in the room in Philadelphia). Maybe both teams are better prepared to wear the crown as presently constituted \u2026 because they clearly weren\u2019t ready last season. Oct. 24 Milwaukee Bucks vs. Houston Rockets (8 p.m. ET, TNT) LA Clippers vs. Golden State Warriors (10:30 p.m. ET, TNT) Why we\u2019re tuning in: The winners of the last five Kia MVP awards will suit up on this night. In Houston, reigning Kia MVP and Bucks dynamo Giannis Antetokounmpo will attempt to crash the debut of the Rockets\u2019 superstar duo of James Harden ( 2018 MVP ) and Westbrook ( 2017 MVP ). Then we top things off with the Clippers visiting the Warriors for the long-awaited opening of the Chase Center in San Francisco. Two-time former Kia MVP winner Stephen Curry ( 2015 and 2016 ) will attempt to lead the patched-up former champs back to the top of the standings without fellow Splash Brother Klay Thompson . We\u2019ll get a full dose of D\u2019Angelo Russell in his Warriors\u2019 debut, though. And we\u2019ll see if the Clippers, who won two games against the Warriors at Oracle Arena in the 2018 playoffs , can make themselves at home in the new spot. Dec. 25 Boston Celtics vs. Toronto Raptors (Noon ET, ESPN) Milwaukee Bucks vs. Philadelphia 76ers (2:30 p.m. ET, ABC) Houston Rockets vs. Golden State Warriors (5 p.m. ET, ABC) LA Clippers vs. Los Angeles Lakers (8 p.m. ET, ESPN\/ABC) New Orleans Pelicans vs. Denver Nuggets (10:30 p.m. ET, ESPN) Why we\u2019re tuning in: Five marquee matchups on one day, the biggest and arguably the best single day of showcase games on the schedule, gives us a little bit of everything. Superstars, All-Stars, future stars and contenders from both sides of the conference divide. The Nuggets promise to be one of the most interesting teams to watch this season as we will all see if their No. 2 finish in the West last season was was a preview of more to come \u2026 or something else. The Warriors and Rockets rarely disappoint. The same can be said for the Clippers and Lakers and the Celtics and Raptors in recent seasons. But the Bucks and Sixers might deliver the most intriguing matchup of the day with Antetokounmpo and Joel Embiid both looking to settle any lingering questions about who runs the Eastern Conference. * * * Sekou Smith is a veteran NBA reporter and NBA TV analyst. "},{"id":32283,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/nba-schedule-release-earlier-starts-fewer-back-backs","date":"2019-08-12","title":"NBA schedule features earlier tipoffs, fewer back-to-backs","content":" (AP) \u2014 The NBA schedule is a little bit easier on players. Fans might be catching a break \u2014 and some more sleep \u2014 as well. The league announced its 2019-20 schedule on Monday , featuring another dip in back-to-back games for teams and a major change in the number of nationally televised games starting at 10:30 p.m. on the East coast. Golden State and the Los Angeles Lakers will start several games a half-hour earlier than usual, while broadcasters ESPN and Turner are going to earlier start times on many of their midweek doubleheader nights. Such a change has been on NBA Commissioner Adam Silver\u2019s mind for some time, especially since roughly half of the nation\u2019s television homes are in the East time zone \u2014 but now, a number of the league\u2019s biggest stars play on the West coast. It wasn\u2019t uncommon for nationally televised midweek games to end around 1 a.m. or even later last season, and that was not good for ratings. \u201cIt\u2019s something that I think we have to address,\u201d Silver said in May. And changes are definitely coming. ESPN\u2019s Wednesday doubleheaders \u2014 mostly at 8 and 10:30 p.m. last season \u2014 will begin at either 7 or 7:30 p.m., followed by a second game at either 9:30 p.m. or 10 p.m. in the East. TNT had nine Tuesday doubleheaders last season with the second game starting at 10:30; this season that number is down to two, with the second game now mostly starting at 9:30 or 10 p.m. In all, there were 57 games on national television starting at 10:30 p.m. last season. That number falls to 33 this season, a dip of 42 percent. Meanwhile, players might be getting a touch more rest this season as well. For the fifth straight year, the NBA has found a way to lower the average number of times a team has to play on consecutive days. The league average is 12.4 back-to-backs this season, down from 13.3 last year and 36 percent down from the average of 19.3 five years ago. Other highlights from the 2019-20 schedule: OPENING NIGHT Toronto will get its rings on Oct. 22, when it plays host to New Orleans and No. 1 overall pick Zion Williamson. The Lakers \u2014 now featuring Anthony Davis to play alongside LeBron James \u2014 will play at the Clippers \u2014 now featuring Kawhi Leonard and Paul George \u2014 in the second half of that doubleheader, and that will be one of the 10:30 p.m. Eastern nationally televised midweek games that will otherwise be largely avoided this season. CHRISTMAS Toronto gets to host a Christmas game for the first time, playing host to Boston at noon Eastern. The other Christmas matchups (all times Eastern): Milwaukee at Philadelphia, 2:30 p.m.; Houston at Golden State, 5 p.m.; Clippers at Lakers, 8 p.m.; New Orleans at Denver, 10:30 p.m. MARTIN LUTHER KING DAY There are 14 games scheduled for Jan. 20, the day honoring the life of Dr. Martin Luther King Jr., including the traditional home games for Atlanta (against Toronto) and Memphis (against New Orleans). EUROPE IN PRIME TIME The schedule features 48 games \u2014 24 on Saturdays, 24 on Sundays \u2014 that will air in prime time in Europe. That doesn\u2019t include the Jan. 24 game in Paris between Milwaukee and Charlotte. FOUR-IN-FIVES The stretches of four games in five days might be gone for good. This will be the third consecutive season where no team gets tasked with handling one of those. No team will play eight games in 12 days, either \u2014 though there are 19 instances of teams having to play five times in a span of seven days. CLOSING NIGHT The regular season ends with 13 games on April 15. Miami, Detroit, Denver and Utah all finish on April 14. The playoffs start April 18."},{"id":32254,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/best-moments-2019-nba-rookie-photoshoot","date":"2019-08-12","title":"Best moments from Panini NBA Rookie Photo Shoot","content":" The 2019 NBA rookie class gathered in New Jersey for the annual Panini NBA Rookie Photo Shoot on Sunday. After the Senior Team beat the Select Team 97-78 in the scrimmage, two players on the Senior Team were replaced by two players from the Select Team for the next phase of training camp \u2014 three practices and an exhibition game against Spain in Los Angeles. Sent home from the Senior Team were center Bam Adebayo and forward Thaddeus Young. The 22-year-old Adebayo was one of the best rebounders in camp, but was probably a little too raw in comparison to the other bigs. Young, meanwhile, didn\u2019t provide the shooting that the remaining power forwards on the roster do. Added to the roster in their place were Marvin Bagley III and Derrick White, who impressed as members of Jeff Van Gundy\u2019s Select Team. However, after being promoted to the Senior Team, Bagley decided to withdraw from the competition to focus on the upcoming NBA season. White will join the 13 other healthy players from the Senior Team, along with Kyle Lowry (who is recovering from thumb surgery and missed all of this week\u2019s camp) and Marcus Smart (who missed the last three days with a sore left calf). From those 16 players, a 12-man roster will be selected for the World Cup. That roster doesn\u2019t need to be finalized until a two days before the tournament begins on Aug. 31, a fact that USA Basketball managing director Jerry Colangelo has brought up multiple times this week. So he and the rest of the staff clearly won\u2019t rush a final decision and it\u2019s possible that the team will take more than 12 players with it from Los Angeles to Australia, where it will play three more exhibition games before heading to China. \u201cWe\u2019re going to be patient with the rest of the squad, because we have plenty of time,\u201d Colangelo said Friday. \u201cWe want to make sure everyone gets a real shot, and I think the staff is sorting through all that. There\u2019s something we like about every one of the players.\u201d Both Lowry and Smart are likely to make the final roster if they\u2019re healthy, but the status of both is still very much in the air. Lowry is expected to be reevaluated by his doctor before the start of the L.A. camp, and Smart will see how he feels after a few days off. Other sure things to make the final roster are Jayson Tatum (Friday\u2019s leading scorer) and four of the five starters from the scrimmage: Kemba Walker, Donovan Mitchell, Jaylen Brown and Khris Middleton, though Senior Team head coach Gregg Popovich said afterward that inferring too much into the starting lineup would be \u201can incorrect assumption.\u201d \u201cWe\u2019re still trying to figure out how people fit together,\u201d he continued. \u201cYou don\u2019t always necessarily play your most talented guys together. It\u2019s got to be a good mix. You got to have something coming off the bench also. What we\u2019re doing now is just mixing and matching and taking a look at everybody.\u201d The status of guards De\u2019Aaron Fox (who had 12 points and three steals on Friday), Joe Harris and White could depend on the health of Lowry and Smart. The frontline may have more questions than answers. Harrison Barnes is a pretty safe bet to make the roster, maybe leaving one roster spot between Kyle Kuzma and P.J. Tucker. The competition at center features Brook Lopez, Mason Plumlee and Myles Turner, who was the Senior Team\u2019s starting center on Friday. \u201cThere are going to be some players that are more talented than others, but a lot of jobs have to be filled,\u201d Popovich said. \u201cOverall, we\u2019re looking for people who are committed defensively and are totally unselfish and are willing to move the ball and move themselves at the offensive end.\u201d With the Senior Team scoring just once on is first six possessions and with the Select Team bigs feasting inside, the young guys jumped out to an 8-2 lead on Friday. But the Senior Team got some stops and the second unit \u2014 Fox, Harris, Tatum, Kuzma and Lopez \u2014 took the lead for good with a 9-0 run to close the first quarter. The Select Team scored just 28 points over the second and third periods and it was a 30-point game going into the fourth. Credit the Senior Team defense (which mixed in some 2-3 zone), though it should be noted that the Select Team was lacking shooters (it finished 3-for-26 from 3-point range) and running plays that they\u2019d seen all week. Tatum was the offensive star, scoring a game-high 17 points on 6-for-8 shooting in just 15:44 off the bench. His biggest highlight on Friday was a late-third-quarter spin move to a left-handed scoop in traffic. But he has shot well most of the week, looking to be in midseason form despite not having played an NBA game in almost three months. \u201cI just tried to come in the best shape as I could,\u201d he said. \u201cI just tried to get in a rhythm before I got out here.\u201d Though Popovich was quick to dismiss Friday\u2019s starting lineup as non-news, it\u2019s easy to see Tatum staying in that sixth man role, where he could provide some scoring punch off the bench. \u201cHe was very aggressive tonight,\u201d Popovich said. \u201cWe really like that about him and need that from him.\u201d A foundation has been set. But there\u2019s still a long way to go before this team is ready for real competition. Developing chemistry, so that the talent can really flourish within the system, takes time. \u201cEverybody here is really talented and has a high IQ,\u201d Tatum said. \u201cWe all know how to play basketball. We did a lot of great things on the fly today, but it\u2019s going to get better with time.\u201d * * * John Schuhmann is a senior stats analyst for NBA.com. Jayson Tatum scored 17 points for the Blue, which got 14 from Kemba Walker and 12 from De\u2019Aaron Fox. Everybody who was supposed to play did, new U.S. coach Gregg Popovich got to tinker with a lot of combinations and no one got seriously hurt \u2014 thankfully, there was no reprise of the scene like the one five years ago during a USA Basketball exhibition game in Las Vegas, when Paul George suffered a horrible lower leg injury. John Collins also scored 12 and Jonathan Isaac added 11 points for the White squad. The tournament starts Aug. 31 and the Americans open group play on Sept. 1 against the Czech Republic in Shanghai. Tucker, Mason Plumlee, Adebayo and Young eventually got worked in. \u201cI think it\u2019s incumbent on the staff to figure out the best combinations as far as roles are concerned,\u201d Popovich said. The Blue led by as many as 30. Lowry, the point guard for the NBA champion Toronto Raptors told NBA TV during the game that he will meet with his surgeon, Dr. Michelle Carlson from the Hospital for Special Surgery, on Monday \u2014 at which time he may know when he can return to action. Lowry, who had surgery last month to repair a torn tendon in his left thumb, is hoping to participate in national team workouts next week. \u201cHopefully she gives me some good news,\u201d Lowry said. He\u2019s been in a splint for about four weeks. Former USA Basketball coach Mike Krzyzewski and his wife Mickie were courtside. Krzyzewski led the Americans to an 88-1 record and five gold medals \u2014 three Olympics, two World Cups \u2013 in his 12 years at the helm before being succeeded by Popovich for this Olympic cycle. Also in attendance was Vegas regular Floyd Mayweather, a big basketball fan, along with U.S. Olympic basketball gold medalists Sam Perkins and Chris Mullin. After practices next week, the U.S. will play Spain in an exhibition at Anaheim, California on Aug. 16 before flying to Australia the next day. "},{"id":32314,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/qa-boston-celtics-legend-bob-cousy","date":"2019-08-09","title":"Q&A: Bob Cousy reflects on his life, NBA career, Bill Russell and more","content":" Bob Cousy turned 91 on Aug. 9, but it ranked no higher than second as far as big deals for him this month. On Aug. 22, Cousy will visit the White House to receive the Presidential Medal of Freedom from President Donald Trump. It ranks with the Congressional Gold Medal as the highest civilian award and typically is bestowed for \u201cmeritorious contribution to the security or national interests of the United States, world peace, cultural or other significant public or private endeavors.\u201d Honored recipients are chosen from across all fields, from business and economics, politics and academia to religion, the arts, science, philosophy and medicine. Cousy will become the 33rd recipient from the sports world. What the legendary Boston Celtics guard is most proud of, in receiving the medal, is that it recognizes contributions outside of his athletic career. Cousy\u2019s Celtics\u2019 career was remarkable \u2014 six NBA championships in seven years from 1957-62, 13 All-Star selections in 13 seasons, a first-ballot selection to the Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame and acclaim as the both the league\u2019s prototypical point guard and a major gate attraction with his clever, behind-the-back passing and peripheral court vision. > NBA History:   A closer look at Cousy\u2019s career But the 6-foot-1 guard from Holy Cross was the spark behind the formation and acceptance of the National Basketball Players Association, the union that has made partners of NBA team owners and players while generating the top salaries in major U.S. sports. He also helped to usher black teammates \u2014 including pioneer Chuck Cooper, Bill Russell, Sam Jones, K.C. Jones and Satch Sanders \u2014 as well as the Boston team, the league and their fans through racial integration in the 1950s and \u201860s as America\u2019s civil rights lights were blinking on. Cousy spoke with NBA.com\u2019s Steve Aschburner about his upcoming White House visit, as well as his illustrious career. Here is part of that conversation. (For more on Cousy\u2019s remarkable career, check out 10 Things To Know . * * * Steve Aschburner: Congratulations on the honor and your upcoming trip to the White House. What do you make of it, being chosen to receive the Presidential Medal of Freedom, and why is it happening now? Bob Cousy: The story is, three or four good friends came to me about four years ago and asked if I was prepared to perhaps be a recipient, and did I want them to pursue it? I told them I really had never pursued that type of acknowledgement before. But I also didn\u2019t tell them \u201cNo.\u201d So they went out with their plan. Congressman Jim McGovern [D-Mass.] agreed to help them. They put a portfolio together. We thought we had a pretty strong case to make to President Obama. We had a letter that President Kennedy had written to me. We got letters from [former Massachusetts governor] Deval Patrick and [Senator] Cory Booker [D-N.J.], but at the end of the day it didn\u2019t happen. I became involved and reached out to a friend of mine \u2014 who is Senator Joe Manchin\u2019s [D-WVa.] closest friend, I guess \u2014 and he reached out to Joe. And Joe is an honest politician who follows his conscience. SA: Oh, he\u2019s the one \u2026 BC: He\u2019s a Democrat who doesn\u2019t rely on a particular ideology or party affiliation to make decisions. He makes them on their merits. I\u2019ve tried to do the same thing my entire life. My wife and I were registered independents for 63 years for that reason. We didn\u2019t want to get locked into ideology, where everything that came up you just voted the same way. That\u2019s what Joe does. Anyway, Joe had an opportunity to help me. The President [Trump] reaches out to Joe from time to time. SA: And it worked? BC: The President called me last Dec. 3, with he and Joe having lunch together at the White House. Joe had given him my portfolio and, despite the fact it was kind of Democratically tinged, he obviously thought it had merit and he offered me the medal to be given in April. I obviously accepted \u2014 we had a nice 15-minute dialogue \u2014 and I did say, \u2018Mr. President, I am flattered by you calling personally. But I told Joe a year ago I\u2019d refuse to accept this award posthumously.\u2019 He laughed at that and said, \u201cI\u2019m going to do it again in April and you\u2019re the first one I\u2019m inviting.\u201d He said, \u201cSo can you stay alive till April.\u201d I told him I\u2019d give it my best shot. SA: But it didn\u2019t happen in April, did it? BC: A guy named Tiger did something spectacular [Tiger Woods won the Masters golf tournament with a stirring comeback performance]. So the President delayed my presentation because he wanted to do Tiger immediately. Shortly after that, his aide contacted me and said, \u201cOK, the President would like to make it on July 29.\u201d I said, \u201cOooh, that\u2019s only two weeks away. Do we have a Plan B?\u201d She said, \u201cSure. How \u2018bout August 22.\u201d I said \u201cBingo! I\u2019ll be there with bells on.\u201d SA: Will you be honored with other recipients? BC: No. He\u2019s the first President \u2014 my ace son-in-law investigated this back to [former President Harry] Truman, and it\u2019s always been done in one ceremony once a year in November. It usually focuses on the arts, but they throw in a few jocks. President Trump is the first one that has decided, instead of one ceremony, he is going to stagger \u2018em. He did, I think, [auto racing giant] Roger Penske in June and [economist] Art Laffer in July, and then I\u2019m up for August. He told me he liked doing it so he didn\u2019t want to do them all together. I was told I\u2019ll be the only recipient on August 22 in the Oval Office. SA: How exciting is this for you and your loved ones? BC: I\u2019ve had my moment in the sun. I\u2019m the Howard Hughes of the sports world. I\u2019ve done like four appearances in 10 years. I hide pretty well from the media. I\u2019ve taken this occasion to do a few interviews because this came out of the blue, and it\u2019s very meaningful coming at this age. It\u2019s a completion of a life\u2019s circle for me, and it\u2019s not necessarily related to sports. As he told me when he called, he was reading the portfolio and focused on things I\u2019d done in terms of social justice and other things. SA: Doesn\u2019t ever get boring, eh, being honored at the White House? BC: I\u2019ve been spoiled. I\u2019ve been to the White House. I\u2019ve been invited six times. I went first in \u201954 when President [Dwight] Eisenhower. Then President [John] Kennedy in \u201963. Then I got the Big Brother of the Year award that was presented by President [Lyndon] Johnson in \u201965. It was nice because he had received it in \u201964. I was heavily involved and still am in Big Brothers. And I went back the next year when they gave the same award to Billy Graham. That was nice, I brought my daughters.  Then I had a small exhibit in the Smithsonian, and President [Ronald] Reagan had a Smithsonian night at the White House. Everyone who had some sort of connection went to that. SA: That\u2019s an impressive \u2014 BC: Wait, let me correct that. President [Richard] Nixon in \u201973 invited us. Believe it or not, we didn\u2019t go to that one. I was coaching a team that beat the Russians, who had beaten us in \u201972 in the Olympics for the first time. The AAU brought a team back, they asked me to coach it, and we beat them four out of six, I think. It got a lot of attention, and President Nixon invited us. It wasn\u2019t a popular thing with the players, though, so I called a team meeting. I said, \u2018Guys, you\u2019re the ones doing all the work here. Am I misreading this or are you not thrilled with going to the White House? If that\u2019s the case, let\u2019s have a show of hands.\u2019 They were mad at Nixon for Vietnam. I didn\u2019t go into the politics of it, I just called the AAU guy in and said, \u201cPlease thank the President profusely. Make whatever apologies you want.\u201d So this is my seventh invitation and, for a lot of reasons, the most exciting. SA: So you and your team were ahead of your time 46 years ago. We have seen instances of sports people or teams turning down White House invitations from the current administration. Did you consider that? BC: Oh no. As I told you, my wife and I were registered independents. To be honest, I didn\u2019t vote for the President. I also didn\u2019t vote for Hillary [Clinton]. I voted for the guy who didn\u2019t know where Aleppo was. [Libertarian POTUS candidate Gary Johnson, in a November 2016 TV interview , couldn\u2019t answer a question about the city at the center of Syrian\u2019s civil war.] However, given this situation, this President will definitely have my vote in 2020. I simply feel, without getting into the politics of it at all, like many Americans \u2014 I agree with some of the things he\u2019s done and disagree with others. SA: From what we see and hear on social and traditional media, there are very few of your type, in the middle. BC: [Laughs] I\u2019m certainly not radicalized at all. I\u2019m upset as most moderates are, I\u2019ve never seen in my 90 years this type of polarization and this vitriolic language that\u2019s being used to oppose anybody. Doesn\u2019t matter whether it\u2019s Donald Trump or anyone, I\u2019m just amazed it\u2019s become so passionate and it\u2019s dividing us as a country. I\u2019m upset about that. I\u2019ve never seen it this bad. But obviously, I\u2019m going to the White House with my family and some close friends, and trying not to make it political in any way. I\u2019m just very pleased to be chosen at this point in my life. SA: Now you and Bill Russell, who received the award in 2011, are legendary teammates who have won this award? BC: There are only two teams in American sports. The Yankees, with Babe Ruth and Yogi Berra. And Russ and I now with the Celtics. For whatever that\u2019s worth to the two teams involved. I hope it\u2019s meaningful to them as well. SA: You witnessed so much of what Russell went through as a proud black athlete during an era when the civil rights battles were beginning. Some of what you have talked about in the past \u2014 intruders breaking into the Russells\u2019 home while they were gone, vandalizing it and defecating in the bed \u2014 was inhuman. What do you make of race relations in the U.S. some 50 or 60 years later? BC: I was saying to someone recently, despite the frenetic and passionate rhetoric on both sides \u2014 and I feel that it is divisive \u2014 I am pleased that we\u2019re having this discussion. Because whether we want to admit it or not \u2014 it\u2019s not that we\u2019re a racist country, I don\u2019t think we are \u2014 but racism exists. We\u2019ve let it sit there. I don\u2019t think we\u2019ve addressed it, certainly not as effectively as we could have. This narrative we\u2019re having now, I see it as perhaps as helping to focus attention on it. For a lot of moderates like myself and those in a position to be helpful, this is helping us to pay attention to it. And maybe something productive and good will come out of that. That\u2019s my hope. SA: Seems like so much time and energy get drained by people yelling at each other, doesn\u2019t it? BC: But if you\u2019ll notice, we\u2019re integrating African-Americans more and more into our culture, certainly in the arts. On television, every other TV ad I see has African-American participation, sometimes completely so, and this is good in my judgment. I\u2019ve traveled all over the world and when you walk the street, you see people of all colors, all ethnicities. After awhile, you don\u2019t even pay attention to it because it\u2019s normal. And what I just cited, this is how you normalize it. Hopefully, eventually, we\u2019ll have the same reaction. We won\u2019t notice who\u2019s white, who\u2019s a tinge of another color. That\u2019s the way it should be. SA: You\u2019ve said you regret not speaking out on Russell\u2019s behalf more when you were teammates [1956-63] and wish you\u2019d had more meaningful conversations with him on race. That\u2019s noted in Gary M. Pomerantz\u2019s book, \u201cThe Last Pass\u201d about the two of you. But Russell was sometimes criticized for being aloof and angry. He is very prideful and did not suffer fools gladly. How did you see it? BC: Russell\u2019s a very sensitive black man who resented any type of racism he endured. He decided to fight the battle in his way. I would not judge. You know, athletes are competitive, and it\u2019s very hard for us to turn the other cheek. And he never did. He made outrageous statements when he had a podium. \u201cBoston is the most racist city in the world,\u201d and things like that. He was trying to get the attention of the majority. That, in his judgment, was his way to fight the good fight. Whether I agreed with that or not. SA: You saw other ways to make the case? BC: I will tell you I had great respect for Arthur Ashe. I remember dropping him a note or two, in terms of how he fought it. He fought it in a different way, without becoming an \u201cUncle Tom\u201d but also without pissing off the moderates. He reached out and tried to do it, I guess, the way Dr. [Martin Luther] King did it: With love. As opposed to Russ\u2019 approach. You\u2019ve got to follow your instincts in something like that. I had great respect for Arthur Ashe in how he fought the battle. But I would never criticize Russ for how his instincts told him he had to fight his battle. SA: What are your thoughts on the NBA, which is considered the most progressive of the major sports leagues? BC: One of the things that makes me the most proud is, I started the NBA players association in 1955. In those days, there were only six franchises, then we went to eight and 10. You had to plead with people to come in, you\u2019d give away tickets. Fast-forward 50 or 60 years, and the last time I looked, they sold a franchise in L.A. for $2.1 billion. That\u2019s with a \u201cb.\u201d That\u2019s how far a league has come that we set the table for in the 1950s. I\u2019m proud that I played a role. SA: What was the key to making that work? BC: Part of it was the NBA Board of Governors living harmoniously with the NBA Players Association. In terms of what we just spoke about \u2014 the radicalization of politics in this country and the division that\u2019s involved \u2014 that was just the opposite. The reason the NBA has reached the levels they\u2019ve reached in this period of time is, the commissioners maybe weren\u2019t kissy-poo \u2014 I\u2019m sure there were harsh words \u2014 but in the end the player and the NBA governors worked together toward their common good. And the good of everyone involved. SA: So no resentment or envy of today\u2019s players and the salaries they command? BC: [Laughs] I used to say when I spoke, \u201cI was the highest paid player in the league in 1963, I made $35,000. Isn\u2019t that great?\u201d Forty years later, a guy named Michael was the best guard in the league and made $35 million. And last year, LeBron made $40 million for one year. So I am pleased I made a small role in setting the table for this kind of organization. Now people like Adam Silver, and David Stern before him, continue this legacy, I think, of working harmoniously with the \u201cother side\u201d if you want to call them that. Seems to me they\u2019ve all worked together to create this NBA entity we\u2019re all proud of. * * * Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. For the scrimmage, the Blue Team will be the 15 healthy players on the Senior Team Roster (with Kyle Lowry and Marcus Smart injured), while the White Team will be the 11 remaining players on the Select Team roster (with Trae Young having left camp with his own injury). In training camps of years past, Senior Team guys have been split up for the final-night scrimmage. Doing that again would allow for more playing time for everyone, but the Senior Team and Select Team (coached by Jeff Van Gundy) have been operating separately all week and not running the same stuff. This is the last chance for guys (on either team) to earn a trip to Los Angeles for the next phase of training camp, which begins Tuesday night. And for that, it should be a pretty competitive game. \u201cThe thing that I love is our intensity in practice,\u201d Kemba Walker said Thursday. \u201cWe\u2019re getting after it, every possession, every drill. The communication level is so high.\u201d The Senior Team lineups and playing-time distribution will be very interesting. The plan (which could change) is to announce the trimmed down roster for the L.A. camp on Saturday morning. That roster will likely have at least 15 names on it, but the roster math goes beyond the 15 Senior Team guys who are healthy, and there will surely be some cuts. Here are some thoughts and questions regarding the roster\u2026 The closest thing to a certainty with this roster is that the starting backcourt will be Walker and Donovan Mitchell. The two have played together quite a bit in camp, Mitchell has looked like a budding star, and it\u2019s fair to say that Walker has enjoyed the partnership. \u201cI love playing with that kid,\u201d Walker said. \u201cHe\u2019s such a competitor. He\u2019s so intense. He reminds me of myself a lot. I love it. It\u2019s going to be fun playing with him.\u201d And in regard to Mitchell\u2019s ability to play the two, Walker has no doubts. \u201cEasily,\u201d Walker answered. \u201cThat kid is so talented, and he wants it. That\u2019s what I love the most.\u201d The status of Lowry (recovering from thumb surgery) and Smart (sore left calf) hang over this whole process. We\u2019ll know more about both of them next week, but in deciding who\u2019s going to L.A., the USA staff has to plan for the possibility that neither will be on the World Cup roster. Lowry is obviously the more doubtful of the two. Other players (whose NBA seasons finished a lot earlier than June 13) have backed out for reasons far less severe than thumb surgery. So give the NBA champ (and 2016 Olympic gold medalist) a ton of credit for just being here. And even if he isn\u2019t on the World Cup roster, Lowry\u2019s presence and clear desire to play will surely earn him some equity in regard to the selection of next year\u2019s Olympic team. De\u2019Aaron Fox and Joe Harris were promoted from the Select Team to the Senior Team before camp even started. Could another player or two leap-frog some Senior Team players and earn an invite to L.A.? Based on impressions from the last three days, Derrick White would be the No. 1 candidate. White would still be behind Walker, Mitchell and (probably) Lowry\/Fox in the ball-handler\u2019s depth chart, but with Trae Young (eye infection) not playing on Friday, White will have a better opportunity to shine than some guys on the Senior Team. Jalen Brunson is the only other healthy ball-handler on the Select Team. Marvin Bagley III has also drawn a lot of praise in camp, and the depth chart on the Senior Team frontline appears to be wide open. The Select Team roster is big-heavy and Bagley will be sharing playing time with Jarrett Allen, John Collins, Jaren Jackson Jr. and Mitchell Robinson on Friday. But if USA Basketball managing director Jerry Colangelo and Senior Team coach Gregg Popovich want to get another good look at Bagley, Van Gundy will surely oblige. Both Jaylen Brown and Jayson Tatum are pretty safe bets to make the final roster, and there\u2019s a chance they could be the starting forwards. Tatum shot very well in the controlled scrimmage that the media watched on Thursday, and Brown is arguably the most versatile forward in camp. Kyle Kuzma offers similar versatility, and it will be interesting to see where he stands in the rotation on Friday. Khris Middleton is one of only three 2019 All-Stars on the 17-man roster, but hasn\u2019t stood out in scrimmages. Joe Harris, meanwhile, hasn\u2019t been the best shooter. Middleton should get by on his resume, but there may be some pressure on Harris in Friday\u2019s scrimmage. \u201cObviously, you hope to make shots,\u201d Harris said Thursday. \u201cBut you can\u2019t put too much pressure on yourself to make it, because whether or not they go in, you\u2019re creating space everybody else. That\u2019s what you want, especially in settings like this, where everybody\u2019s got a tendency to pack in [defensively] so much. If you\u2019ve got one guy that can create just a little bit of space for somebody that can get downhill, it opens up everything offensively.\u201d For a few minutes of Thursday\u2019s controlled scrimmage, we saw a two-center frontcourt of Myles Turner and Brook Lopez. And we also saw a couple of no-center frontcourts: Harrison Barnes with P.J. Tucker and Kuzma with Thaddeus Young. Barnes and Young would seemingly be in direct competition for a roster spot. For now, give Barnes the edge because of his experience with the 2016 Olympic team and his superior 3-point shooting. \u201cYou got to have enough shooters,\u201d Colangelo said earlier this week, \u201cso guys that can shoot the ball have a little bit of an edge, all [other] things being equal.\u201d If the roster includes four guards (Walker, Mitchell and two of the following group: Fox, Harris, Lowry, Smart and White), they have eight roster spots left. If four of those are 3\/4 guys (Brown, Kuzma, Middleton and Tatum), they have four spots for bigger forwards and centers. Would they take Barnes (or Young), Tucker and two centers? Would they remove Kuzma from the 3\/4 group and add a third center? Three centers seems like a lot, but some of the best teams at the world cup have NBA talent up front: Nikola Jokic for Serbia, Marc Gasol for Spain, Rudy Gobert for France, Andrew Bogut and Aron Baynes for Australia, and Domantas Sabonis and Jonas Valanciunas for Lithuania. In that regard, a question that could come up in staff deliberations: Is there a player that they would want for one specific matchup? For instance, while Lopez and Turner are superior rim protectors and offensive players, neither would necessarily be the best option to defend Jokic in a matchup against Serbia (arguably the second best team in the tournament). According to Second Spectrum matchup data , Jokic scored at a higher rate than usual when defended by both of those guys last season, shooting 31-for-58 (53 percent) on 197 total possessions against the two. Might the best option in a Jokic matchup be his own teammate? Mason Plumlee doesn\u2019t offer much offensively, but he\u2019s a player that coaches can trust, he\u2019s more mobile defensively than either Lopez or Turner, and he obviously knows Jokic well. Along those same lines, is there a player on this roster who\u2019s best suited to defend Giannis Antetokounmpo? Tucker had some success in that regard last season, holding the MVP to just 20 points on 98 possessions as his primary defender. In fact, among the 16 players who defended Antetokounmpo for at least 60 possessions last season, Tucker is the one who held him furthest below his regular scoring rate . (Jabari Parker was next on the list, so hey, let\u2019s not take that data for gospel.) The U.S. will likely play Greece in the second round of pool play (before the single-elimination tournament). There will be three players in the World Cup who received MVP votes last season, and none of the three will be playing for the United States. Per ESPN\u2019s Brian Windhorst , Young suffered a minor eye infection and will leave the camp, which is being held in Las Vegas. Although I look forward to seeing [USA Basketball National Team] Coach [Gregg] Popovich and the Team bring home the Gold this summer, I feel it is most important for me at this moment in my career to focus on my health and preparing for the NBA season with the Atlanta Hawks. Finally, I want to thank USA Basketball and I look forward to hopefully having another opportunity in the future!\u201d Young\u2019s teammate on the Hawks, big man John Collins, is still participating in the camp as a part of the Select Team. Additionally, Hawks coach Lloyd Pierce is serving as an assistant coach for the USA Basketball National Team as a part of Popovich\u2019s staff. And the media walked in to see the young guys finish off a 22-6 quarter to close practice. The Select Team actually started practicing on Sunday, so they\u2019ve had an extra day together. Their job is to prepare the Senior Team for how opponents will play them at the World Cup. Only three of the 17 players on the main roster have played FIBA basketball on the senior level. So part of the agenda for this week is getting players used to the rule differences and style of play. The biggest rule difference is the lack of a defensive three-second rule. That could be advantageous for the U.S., with two of the league\u2019s best rim protectors \u2014 Brook Lopez and Myles Turner \u2014 potentially on the roster. But it will also make it tougher to get to the basket on offense than guys are used to. So the Select Team was crowding the paint on Tuesday. The staff has also showed the players film from previous tournaments to emphasize the lack of driving lanes. \u201cThere\u2019s not as much freedom to get down the lane,\u201d Joe Harris said Tuesday. \u201cA lot of teams are going to be overloading and packing it in, and you got to be able to knock down shots.\u201d That obviously helps Harris\u2019 chances of making the World Cup roster, even though the league\u2019s leading 3-point shooter from last season (47.4 percent) wasn\u2019t on the Senior Team roster until Monday. Harrison Barnes (27th at 39.5 percent) is the only other player on the 17-man roster that finished the top 40 in 3-point percentage. New U.S. coach Gregg Popovich wants the ball to move. This team has a \u201cpoint-five-second rule\u201d on offense, where players shouldn\u2019t hold the ball for more than half a second before doing something with it. Every half of a second where the ball is held makes it tougher to get a good shot. (The FIBA shot clock is the same as it is in the NBA \u2014 24 seconds, with a reset to 14 after an offensive rebound.) Mason Plumlee is one of the three guys here who played under coach Mike Krzyzewski for a previous version of the Senior Team. And the emphasis on ball movement is also about the new coach. \u201cCoach K ran a lot of the stuff we ran at Duke,\u201d Plumlee said. \u201cPop is definitely San Antonio-style of play where it\u2019s no-hold basketball. You\u2019re moving it.\u201d It\u2019s also about the make-up of the roster, which doesn\u2019t include any of the 15 American players who averaged at least three isolation possessions per game last season . \u201cIn the past,\u201d Barnes explained, \u201cthe one-on-one talent itself has been so potent \u2014 Kobe, LeBron, Durant, Carmelo \u2014 guys can go out there and get a basket. This year, with the experience that other teams are going to have over us, how hard we play is going to have to carry the day.\u201d For Barnes, camp has had a much different feel than when he was preparing for the 2016 Olympics with a very different group. \u201cIn \u201916, I was one of the younger guys on the team,\u201d he said. \u201cIt was more of a veteran team. People knew how to play. They had already been through the system and the pipeline. It was more so just make sure you\u2019re in shape, make sure everyone\u2019s healthy, and just go out there and play. \u201cThis time around, it\u2019s much more structured. You can tell that Pop really wants to put his imprint on USA Basketball. With how the young the team is, the teaching is much more the emphasis.\u201d Defense might require a bigger adjustment for some of these players, because they\u2019re used to certain principles with their NBA teams and will have to put those aside to defend (and call out coverages) according to the U.S. Team\u2019s standards. The staff is anticipating a lot of pick-and-rolls from their opponents, and they want to defend those pick-and-rolls with just two defenders. \u201cWe\u2019re doing some different stuff on defense,\u201d Plumlee said, \u201cto try to guard the pick-and-roll with two players and stay home with shooters.\u201d And Popovich hasn\u2019t hesitated to take these NBA vets back to the basics. Both Barnes and Harris mentioned the \u201cshell drill,\u201d used to work on defensive positioning with the movement of the ball. But there hasn\u2019t been too many drills. The first two practices have featured a lot of scrimmaging. On Monday, it was the 16 healthy Senior Team guys split into two eight-player squads, and on Tuesday, the Select Team was brought in. With only 21 days of training before the first World Cup game (vs. the Czech Republic on Sept. 1), there\u2019s not much time to build chemistry between guys who aren\u2019t used to playing alongside one another. \u201cYou can script and walk through stuff,\u201d Plumlee said, \u201cbut playing is the best way to get a feel for your teammates.\u201d \u201cIt\u2019s all new for everybody,\u201d Khris Middleton added. \u201cThe first thing is to learn the principles. Try to learn each one of these guys out here. In order to accomplish our goal, we got to figure out things quickly and try to get on the same page as soon as we can.\u201d * * * John Schuhmann is a senior stats analyst for NBA.com. But he was allowed in at a second entry point after providing identification. Players on the Brooklyn Nets, Houston Rockets, Los Angeles Lakers and Toronto Raptors will have even less than that, along with a trip back to Asia for early-October exhibition games in Japan or China.
