experiences is available on the App Store for download today, and includes new training drills featuring Nash, and winner of the 2019 MTN DEW 3-Point Contest , Joe Harris of the Brooklyn Nets."},{"id":32685,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/25-days-reshaped-league","date":"2019-07-11","title":"How a span of 25 days altered the NBA landscape","content":"Editor\u2019s Note: The evening after NBA.com published this story, the NBA\u2019s wild offseason ride continued with the reported Russell Westbrook-Chris Paul trade. * * * LAS VEGAS \u2013 So maybe it didn\u2019t boast the same drama and shock value as \u201cThe Day The Earth Stood Still.\u201d As far as historical significance and political turmoil, socialist-journalist John Reed\u2019s account a century ago of the October Revolution in Russia, \u201cTen Days That Shook the World,\u201d generated far more controversy. But within the context of sports and certainly relative to its own offseason history, what the NBA just put itself, its principals and its fans through qualifies as nothing less than \u201c25 Days That Reshaped the League.\u201d It wasn\u2019t just what happened, though, that was profound. Star players relocating, general managers scrambling, media reports flying, owners exhausting their checkbooks, a dynasty punting, and old rivals recruiting new teammates. It wasn\u2019t merely the breakneck pace, though that was breathtaking. Kevin Durant shockingly went to the floor with a torn Achilles tendon on June 10, the date of Game 5 of The Finals at Toronto\u2019s Scotiabank Arena. On July 5, just three-and-a-half weeks later, Finals MVP Kawhi Leonard announced he would be taking his trophies to southern California, specifically to the Los Angeles Clippers. And, oh yeah, All-Star wing Paul George of the Oklahoma City Thunder would be joining him. Twenty-five days from start to finish. That last maneuver even upstaged an earthquake that rattled the first night of the Las Vegas Summer League. \u201cWhat happened in that period of time was staggering in how it changed the league,\u201d said David Griffin, new vice president of the New Orleans Pelicans and far from an uninvolved bystander. \u201cYou look at what the Clippers were able to achieve and how quickly it all came together. They were put on the clock, what, 48 hours before they landed the plane? That\u2019s tough.\u201d Dallas owner Mark Cuban, ever the Maverick, questioned the premise. \u201cNothing\u2019s changed,\u201d Cuban said. \u201c[The flurry of activity] was just the nature of how much capital there was.\u201d But Vlade Divac, the Sacramento Kings\u2019 chief basketball exec, exhaled when he considered \u201ca few of those moves\u2026\u201d \u201cIt definitely was interesting. Especially Kawhi, where and when he decided,\u201d Divac said. \u201cEverything was kind of stuck. Not just the NBA but the entire world was waiting to see where he was going to end up.\u201d This was bigger than just the bookends, though. Consider the headlines crammed in between Durant\u2019s injury and Leonard\u2019s decision, and the cumulative ramifications of them. 25 Days between Kevin Duran\u2019t injury (June 10) to Kawhi Leonard\u2019s move to LA (July 5): \u2022 Klay Thompson tears his ACL and, like Durant, will miss much or all of 2019-20. \u2022 Led by Leonard, the Raptors finally bring an NBA championship to Canada. \u2022 Pelicans big man Anthony Davis gets the trade he\u2019d lobbied for, going to the Los Angeles Lakers to play alongside LeBron James. \u2022 Zion Williamson, the mostly highly touted prospect since Davis or maybe James, gets drafted No. 1 by New Orleans. \u2022 Milwaukee\u2019s Giannis Antetokounmpo stakes a claim on the \u201cNBA\u2019s best player\u201d title as the league\u2019s 2019 Most Valuable Player. \u2022 Durant and All-Star point guard Kyrie Irving leave the Warriors and the Celtics, respectively, to team up in Brooklyn. \u2022 The Utah Jazz add both Mike Conley and Bojan Bogdanovic, rock-solid acquisitions for a team amped by the NBA\u2019s newfound parity. \u2022 Jimmy Butler moves via sign-and-trade to the Miami Heat, parting ways with a Philadelphia team he led through two playoff rounds. \u2022\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b But the Sixers fire back, re-signing Tobias Harris, luring Al Horford out of Boston and getting Josh Richardson in the Butler deal. \u2022\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b Golden State \u2013 remember them? \u2013 snatches D\u2019Angelo Russell from Minnesota\u2019s grasp and adds Willie Cauley-Stein. \u2022\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b The earthquake hits the Vegas summer league, shutting down the games and sending spectators into the night. \u2022\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b Then came the Kawhi Bomb, with George as a startling co-star. \u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200bSeriously, that\u2019s enough news and change to carry most sports leagues through an entire calendar year. Yet the NBA burned through those storylines in less than a month. It\u2019s the latest, greatest (in magnitude at least) example of this pro basketball enterprise\u2019s ambitions for global domination, while bigfooting every other sport\u2019s air-time and Web clicks. To some, the frenzy to sign free agents, backfill with replacements and build or rebuild on the fly looked panicked, even unstable. A fan who followed a favorite player\u2019s exploits for a few years unexpectedly faces a choice: switch your allegiance to the player\u2019s new team or re-imagine him from friend to foe by October. It\u2019s the NBA as a full-sized, flesh-and-blood fantasy league. To others, all of this is a natural result of the system negotiated by the teams and the players in their collective bargaining agreement, along with a further shift in power from owners to players as the demand for talent outstrips supply. And then there are the \u201cpotential\u201d junkies, the sort of sports fans who get more excited by signings and trades than they do by the games themselves. Social media has only dialed up the sense of NBA summer as short-attention-span theater. \u201cWhat we\u2019re realizing,\u201d NBA commissioner Adam Silver said Tuesday, \u201cwas that it\u2019s less about pointing fingers. It\u2019s that the world has changed, and in part we\u2019re the victims of our own success. We never used to have this kind of coverage in the offseason. We never used to have this kind of attention to summer league basketball. And as I say, the 24\/7 attention on free agency creates new pressures.\u201d It\u2019s the CBA itself that creates the free agents, though. When the current agreement with the players was negotiated, teams pressed for shorter contracts to save them from debilitating injuries and flawed business decisions. Well, shorter deals mean more players hitting the market sooner and more often, freeing up more salary-cap space in the process. \u201cThey created the conditions for more movement,\u201d one former team executive said this week. \u201cNow we\u2019re seeing that. And there were so many big names out there this summer, which hasn\u2019t happened often. In 2016, there was more money [from a flood of TV rights fees] but there weren\u2019t as many blockbuster names.\u201d Said Silver: \u201c[Shorter contracts] create more of a sense of urgency with players. It creates greater incentives for performance. \u2026 We didn\u2019t do it to create more interest in the offseason, but obviously it\u2019s created extraordinary media interest and fan interest. For the most part, that\u2019s been something that\u2019s positive.\u201d The NBA sees the hyperactivity in June and July as a net gain, with an audience excited by the comings and goings greater than however many people might be turned off by the dollar amounts tossed around or the vast game of market musical chairs. Still, there are downsides. Leonard\u2019s move to L.A. might have given some Toronto fans the bends, taking them from the euphoria of the franchise\u2019s first title in its 24-year existence, then plunging them to traumatic emotional depths with his departure. \u201cThink about what it means if you\u2019re Toronto,\u201d one NBA GM said. \u201cYou built a championship team \u2013 and that didn\u2019t matter. He wanted to leave. What do you do? Literally, what\u2019s the answer? It\u2019s not championships. It\u2019s not maintaining their health. They have all the power.\u201d Then there are the folks in OKC, minding their own business before Leonard\u2019s pitch to George prompted the Thunder player to suddenly ask to be traded. \u201cThere are always those unintended consequences, right?\u201d the former exec said. \u201cThe teams wanted shorter contracts but this is the flip side of that \u2013 you can\u2019t lock guys in either. \u201cIf a guy\u2019s on a six-year deal and demands to be traded after two, it\u2019s more like, \u2018Haha! Sure.\u2019 But when they start having leverage is when they get closer to the expiration.\u201d Said a GM: \u201cUnfortunately free agency now exists even for players under contract.\u201d Davis got close enough with the Pelicans to join James \u2013 with whom he also shares an agent, Rich Paul \u2013 on the Lakers. George was close enough, too, given reality that OKC was carrying an exorbitant payroll, paying massive luxury taxes and not advancing past the playoffs\u2019 first round. One rival GM said it was an open secret that the Thunder\u2019s Sam Presti was going to make one or more significant roster moves this summer. He still might, based on the speculation about former MVP Russell Westbrook\u2019s future whereabouts. Westbrook\u2019s contract won\u2019t make it easy \u2013 he has four seasons left on the five-year, $205 million extension he signed in 2017, plus a 15 percent trade kicker \u2013 but most league insiders expect him to be moved either soon or during the season. So yeah, Westbrook muddies the time frame of \u201c25 days\u201d a bit, as did Boogie Cousins\u2019 and Rajon Rondo\u2019s deals on day 26 to play for the Lakers. There were other lesser lights who signed, and then this week\u2019s wrinkle in which forward Marcus Morris changed his mind on the verbal assurance he gave San Antonio to pursue a deal with New York. It\u2019s no secret, either, the June 30 starting gun for free agency is only the \u201cofficial\u201d start. No one is being prosecuted for it via tampering fines, but it\u2019s clear there is lots of communication between players, between teams and agents and in every other direction long before deals even leak on Twitter. We\u2019ll stick with June 10 as the start of this madness, though, because of the impact of Durant\u2019s injury on Golden State. Losing both him and Thompson seemed to many as if the Warriors \u2013 truly on the second tier of NBA dynasties with Chicago and San Antonio \u2013 had stepped into an elevator shaft. Eventually their run of five Finals and three titles was going to end. But like that ? Now the entire league is feeling an openness that the Eastern Conference felt a year ago, after LeBron James moved west and took his stranglehold of Finals appearances with him. There either is no favorite in the West or there are a half dozen of them. In the East, the top teams have definitely changed, without any guarantees they\u2019ve gotten better. \u201cAbsolutely. It\u2019s always open,\u201d said Divac, whose Kings want in on some of the lofty aspirations too. \u201cDefinitely it was unfortunate for Golden State \u2013 you never want to have those kind of injuries that shake not just the players, [but] the entire organization and send it a different way. But that\u2019s part of the game.\u201d Said the former team executive: \u201cI do see more parity. It is a lot more wide-open. It reminds me of the 2015 season, the first year Golden State won, where there were five or six in Western Conference that felt they were neck-and-neck.\u201d Asked to name the biggest surprise of the summer so far, several of those interviewed said George\u2019s move to the Clippers, more so than Leonard\u2019s. One insider cited Butler going to Miami, assuming the aggressive All-Star wing wants to be alpha dog on his own team more than a supporting player to Joel Embiid and Ben Simmons. Another GM said it was Durant and Irving teaming up to sign with the Nets. \u201cI don\u2019t think they\u2019re meant to be together in personality or emotionally,\u201d he opined. Almost everybody was surprised by the earthquake that grabbed center stage Friday night, a 7.1 on the Richter scale that started the scoreboard swaying at the Thomas & Mack Center and had courtside fans nervously eyeing the loudspeakers overhead. In the long run, though, in magnitude registered, tremors delivered and aftershocks felt, that shaker might have nothing on the NBA\u2019s tumultuous 25 days. * * * Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. Congratulations to Coach Bertka on this prestigious recognition.\u201d \u201cI am honored and proud to have been selected for the Tex Winter Assistant Coach Lifetime Impact Award by a committee of my coaching peers, said Coach Bill Bertka.\u201d \u201cI am sincerely grateful to the National Basketball Coaches Association for this recognition.\u201d Bertka began his NBA career in 1968 when the Los Angeles Lakers hired him to scout college players for the NBA Draft, making him the first full-time scout in league history. He and his wife, Solveig, had started a college scouting service in the mid-60s and it grew to become an industry leader before shuttering in 1991. Under Head Coach Bill Sharman, Bertka began working with players while also adding advance scouting duties. In 1974 Bertka left the Lakers to become the first General Manager of the New Orleans Jazz. He also served as a Jazz assistant coach under Elgin Baylor. In 1981 when Pat Riley became Head Coach, he brought Bertka back to the Lakers as his first Assistant, and Bertka has worked for the Lakers ever since, as an Assistant Coach, Director of Scouting, Special Assistant to the General Manager and Basketball Consultant. All told, 45 of his 52 years in the NBA have been with the Lakers. He has worked with 17 different Lakers Head Coaches and has coached greats from Wilt Chamberlain and Jerry West to Kareem Abdul-Jabbar and Magic Johnson to Shaquille O\u2019Neal and Kobe Bryant and beyond. He has ten NBA Championship rings and his teams made a total of 20 trips to the NBA Finals. Prior to the NBA, Bertka was a Head Coach at three different colleges, including a four-year stint at his alma mater, Kent State. Bertka, who will turn 92 on August 8, has been inducted into the Santa Barbara Sports Hall of Fame (1989), the Summit County (OH) Sports Hall of Fame (1989), the Kent State University Sports Hall of Fame, (2004) and the Santa Barbara Basketball Court of Champions (2014). \u201cAssistant Coaches often operate behind the scenes and may not receive public recognition for their team\u2019s success. However, if you ask any Head Coach, they would say that their team could not operate without the hard work of these men and women,\u201d said National Basketball Coaches Association Executive Director David S. Fogel. \u201cCoach Bertka certainly exemplifies these values on and off the court, and his tireless work ethic has led to successful seasons throughout his coaching career. Congratulations to Coach Bertka, this honor is well deserved.\u201d The National Basketball Coaches Association Tex Winter Lifetime Achievement Award honors the tremendous achievements and commitment of Hall of Famer Tex Winter, who over an outstanding NBA coaching career set a standard of integrity, competitive excellence, loyalty and tireless promotion of NBA basketball. This year\u2019s award recognizes the extraordinary contributions Bill Bertka has made to the sport throughout his NBA career through building a body of work that has had a positive and powerful impact on the NBA coaching profession. Coach Bertka embodies the high standards and leadership philosophies that Tex Winter brought to the game. The National Basketball Coaches Association Tex Winter Lifetime Impact Award is selected annually by the Award Selection Committee, comprised of some of the most respected coaches and executives in the game, including Rick Adelman, Hubie Brown, Doug Collins, Wayne Embry, Danny Ferry, Mike Fratello, George Karl, Doc Rivers, Rod Thorn and Lenny Wilkens. Prior recipients are Tim Grgurich (2018), Ron Rothstein (2017) and Phil Johnson (2016)."},{"id":32711,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/sixers-sign-al-horford-official-release","date":"2019-07-10","title":"Sixers sign five-time All-Star Al Horford","content":" Philadelphia 76ers General Manager Elton Brand announced today that the team has signed Al Horford. Per team policy, terms of the deal were not disclosed. \u201cWe\u2019re excited to welcome one of the NBA\u2019s best frontcourt players in Al Horford to Philadelphia,\u201d said Brand. \u201cHe has built his reputation around hard work and a tradition of winning, which are the same qualities that have formed the foundation of the 76ers. Among other accolades, Horford was selected to the 2017-18 All-Defensive Second Team and the 2010-11 All-NBA Third Team. For his career, Horford has played in 786 games (782 starts) with Boston and Atlanta and holds averages of 14.1 points, 8.4 rebounds, 3.2 assists and 1.2 blocks in 32.8 minutes per game. It also generated significant discussion among team management and NBA executives during the Board of Governors meeting Tuesday, and dominated the media session afterward with commissioner Adam Silver. The winners and losers of the frenetic player signings and movement won\u2019t be known until the 2019-20 season and beyond. That there were winners and losers, though, was known immediately as stars such as Kevin Durant, Kyrie Irving, Jimmy Butler, Al Horford, Kemba Walker and Kawhi Leonard switched teams. Lots of the talk Tuesday focused on how those outcomes came about, and whether the rules served all of the constituents. \u201cI don\u2019t necessarily see it as player versus owner,\u201d Silver said. \u201cWhen we step back, what\u2019s best for the fan? I think what\u2019s best for the fan is a 30-team league which everyone has the opportunity to compete with a fair set of rules. I think to the extent that the balance of power is out of whack a little bit, we should address it.\u201d  Silver added: \u201cEven this notion of player power, what we\u2019re really talking about is a small group of players.\u201d There were and still are vast ripple effects, though, as second- and third-tier players sought deals or came up empty. Then there was the issue of the so-called moratorium, the period from June 30 to July 6 in which teams, players and their representatives are only supposed to talk and negotiate, without actually inking deals. That generally is viewed as a wink-wink proposition these days. Then there are team identification and continuity issues that arise when as many as 40 percent of the league\u2019s players hit free agency at the same time, as happened this summer. \u201cWe knew when we shortened contracts several years ago that the math [meant] you\u2019re going to have more free agency,\u201d Silver said. \u201cIt\u2019s always a two-edged sword. On one hand, it creates a sense of renewal in a lot of markets. It gives teams an opportunity to rebuild. But the downside, of course, is for other teams, they potentially lose players.\u201d While stating that he didn\u2019t want the league to overreact to one offseason, Silver did say they would explore rules that can be changed unilaterally, while identifying areas that need to be collectively bargained with the players. Another element of this offseason: For the second time in eight months, an MVP-caliber player with years left on his contract told management he wanted to be traded. In December, it was All-Star center Anthony Davis, whose demand and specific desire to land with the Los Angeles Lakers torpedoed the New Orleans Pelicans\u2019 season. Last week, it was Oklahoma City wing Paul George abruptly asking out to join Leonard in a tandem move to the Los Angeles Clippers. While noting that trade demands are nothing new, Silver acknowledged: \u201cIt falls in the same category of issues of the so-called rule of law within a sports league. You have a contract and it needs to be meaningful on both sides. There\u2019s an expectation if you have a contract and it\u2019s guaranteed that the team is going to meet the terms of the contract, and the expectation on the other side is the player is going to meet the terms of the contract. \u201cTrade demands are disheartening. They\u2019re disheartening to the team. They\u2019re disheartening to the community and don\u2019t serve the player well. The players care about their reputations just as much. So that\u2019s an issue that needs to be addressed.\u201d Durant and Irving signed with Brooklyn, leaving Golden State and Boston, respectively. Leonard exited Toronto before the last scrap of confetti was gone from the Raptors\u2019 championship celebration. And though neither the Nets nor the Clippers historically have been free-agent magnets, the bottom line was big names heading to huge markets in New York and California. Next up? Milwaukee and its chances of convincing reigning Kia NBA MVP Giannis Antetokounmpo to sign a mega-deal extension next summer before he can test free agency in 2021. \u201cMy sense in the room today was that we\u2019ve got work to do,\u201d Silver said. \u201cIt\u2019s still the same principles of fair balance of power and a sense that it\u2019s a level playing field. I think that\u2019s what teams want to know. \u201cMy job is to enforce a fair set of rules for all our teams and a set of rules that are clear and make sense for everyone. I think right now we\u2019re not quite there.\u201d Among other topics discussed by the Board of Governors Tuesday and\/or by Silver in his session with reporters: * Even the actual, nitty-gritty game-related news Tuesday \u2013 added opportunities for replay reviews \u2013 could be said to derive from the priority on fairness. Getting referees\u2019 calls right, despite grumbles about in-game delays, drove the addition for this season of a coach\u2019s challenge, as well as reviews triggered directly from the Replay Center in New Jersey. Similar to coaches\u2019 and managers\u2019 ability to request replay in NFL and MLB contests, each NBA team will be entitled to one challenge per game. A team can use it for the following instances: a called personal foul charged to that team; a called out-of-bounds violation, or a called goaltending or basket interference violation. A team must have a timeout available to issue a challenge. And no, there won\u2019t be a flag for each coach to toss as in football; a twirling of the finger, the signal referees currently use, will be sufficient. The challenge system has been in effect for two years in the NBA G League and during Summer League play this year. The Replay Center will initiate reviews immediately this season in deciding 2-point vs. 3-point shots and determining shot-clock violations. An additional courtside administrator will work at the scorer\u2019s table at each game to expedite communication between the game officials and the folks in Secaucus. * Television ratings in the playoffs, down compared to numbers reported in recent years, were not troubling to Silver. \u201cI do not believe, and the data doesn\u2019t support, that it\u2019s from declining interest,\u201d Silver said. \u201cWe have other measurements of social media, fan support [and] attendance that demonstrate that, in fact, interest is growing. And certainly ratings, even conventional ratings, are growing outside of the United States.\u201d A generational shift away from traditional TV viewing, including \u201ccord-cutting,\u201d streaming and even pirating might be at work on NBA ratings. Silver said the changes in media options could mean talks and modifications with the broadcast partners, despite six years remaining on those agreements. \u201cI don\u2019t think there\u2019s anything endemic to the league,\u201d Silver said of the ratings data. \u201cIn fact, at our board meeting we discussed the growth in popularity of the sport, the growth in participation, the fact that we have a young, diverse, global audience. All very positive indicators.\u201d Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. You can e-mail him here , find his archive here and follow him on Twitter . "},{"id":32708,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/nba-board-governors-approves-coachs-challenge","date":"2019-07-10","title":"NBA Board of Governors approves coach's challenge, use of NBA replay center to initiate instant replay","content":" LAS VEGAS   \u2014 The NBA Board of Governors on Tuesday unanimously approved two changes to the instant replay rules. The first change is the introduction of a Coach\u2019s Challenge to trigger instant replay review of a limited set of matters. A version of the Coach\u2019s Challenge that has been in effect in the NBA G League for the last two seasons and is being used at MGM Resorts NBA Summer League 2019 will be adopted in the NBA on a one-year trial basis during the 2019-20 season. The second change enables the NBA Replay Center (in addition to the on-court referees) to trigger instant replay in certain circumstances. This process, which was successfully tested at MGM Resorts NBA Summer League 2018 and is being used again at this year\u2019s event, will be implemented for the 2019-20 NBA season. \u201cThese initiatives further strengthen our officiating program and help referees make the right call,\u201d said NBA President, League Operations Byron Spruell. \u201cGiving head coaches a voice will enhance the confidence in our replay process among teams and fans and add a new, exciting strategic element to our game. Enabling the NBA Replay Center to trigger instant replay will improve game flow and provide real-time awareness of any adjustments to the score.\u201d Coach\u2019s Challenge Key features of the Coach\u2019s Challenge are below: NBA Replay Center Triggers In the first 46 minutes of the game and the first three minutes of overtime, the NBA Replay Center will be able to trigger instant replay of the following events: A new \u201ccourtside administrator,\u201d hired and supervised by the League Office, will be stationed at the scorer\u2019s table to facilitate and expedite communication between the NBA Replay Center and the on-court referees. The courtside administrator will not have any decision-making authority with respect to officiating calls or replay determinations.
